title=".bg">.bg</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Bulgaria</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/\xca\x8c/: &#39;u&#39; in &#39;cut&#39;">\xca\x8c</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="/\xc9\xa1/: &#39;g&#39; in &#39;guy&#39;">\xc9\xa1</span><span title="/\xc9\x9b\xc9\x99r/: &#39;are&#39; in &#39;bare&#39;">\xc9\x9b\xc9\x99r</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">\xc9\x99</span></span>, <wbr /><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/\xca\x8a/: &#39;u&#39; in &#39;push&#39;">\xca\x8a</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span></span>-/</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Bulgaria.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c3/En-us-Bulgaria.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Bulgaria.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span>; <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a>: <span lang="bg">\xd0\x91\xd1\x8a\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb3\xd0\xb0\xd1\x80\xd0\xb8\xd1\x8f</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Bulgarian" title="Romanization of Bulgarian">tr.</a></small> <i><i lang="bg-Latn" title="Bulgarian-language transliteration">B\xc7\x8elgariya</i></i>), officially the <b>Republic of Bulgaria</b> (Bulgarian: <span lang="bg">\xd0\xa0\xd0\xb5\xd0\xbf\xd1\x83\xd0\xb1\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb8\xd0\xba\xd0\xb0 \xd0\x91\xd1\x8a\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb3\xd0\xb0\xd1\x80\xd0\xb8\xd1\x8f</span>, <small>tr.</small> <i><i lang="bg-Latn" title="Bulgarian-language transliteration">Republika B\xc7\x8elgariya</i></i>, <small>IPA:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Bulgarian_and_Macedonian" title="Help:IPA/Bulgarian and Macedonian">[r\xc9\x9b\xcb\x88publik\xc9\x90 b\xc9\x90\xc9\xab\xcb\x88\xc9\xa1arij\xc9\x90]</a></span>), is a country in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Europe" title="Southeast Europe">southeastern Europe</a>. It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Macedonia</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> to the south, and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> to the east. The capital and largest city is <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a>; other major cities are <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv" title="Plovdiv">Plovdiv</a>, <a href="/wiki/Varna" title="Varna">Varna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burgas" title="Burgas">Burgas</a>. With a territory of 110,994 square kilometres (42,855&#160;sq&#160;mi), Bulgaria is Europe\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_countries_by_area" title="List of European countries by area">16th-largest country</a>.\n</p><p>One the earliest societies in the lands of modern-day Bulgaria was the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> <a href="/wiki/Karanovo_culture" title="Karanovo culture">Karanovo culture</a>, which dates back to 6,500 BC. In Antiquity (6th\xe2\x80\x933rd century BC), the region became a battleground for <a href="/wiki/Thracians" title="Thracians">Thracians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persians" class="mw-redirect" title="Persians">Persians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Macedonians" title="Ancient Macedonians">Macedonian Greeks</a> until it was conquered by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> in 45 AD. The Eastern Roman, or Byzantine, Empire lost some of these territories to an invading <a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">Bulgar</a> horde in the late 7th century. The Bulgars then founded the <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">first unified Bulgarian state</a> in 681 AD which dominated most of the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> and significantly influenced <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavic</a> cultures by developing <a href="/wiki/Cyrillic" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyrillic">Cyrillic</a> script. The First Bulgarian Empire lasted until the early 11th century when Byzantine emperor <a href="/wiki/Basil_II" title="Basil II">Basil II</a> conquered and dismantled it. A successful Bulgarian revolt in 1185 established a <a href="/wiki/Second_Bulgarian_Empire" title="Second Bulgarian Empire">Second Bulgarian Empire</a> which reached its apex under <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Asen_II_of_Bulgaria" title="Ivan Asen II of Bulgaria">Ivan Asen II</a> (1218\xe2\x80\x931241). After numerous exhausting wars and feudal strife, the Second Bulgarian Empire disintegrated in 1396 and its territories fell under <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> rule for nearly five centuries. \n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1877%E2%80%9378)" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Turkish War (1877\xe2\x80\x9378)">Russo-Turkish War of 1877\xe2\x80\x9378</a> resulted in the formation of the current Third Bulgarian State. Many ethnic Bulgarian populations were left outside its borders, which led to several conflicts with its neighbours and an alliance with Germany in both world wars. In 1946 Bulgaria became a one-party <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Bulgaria" title="People&#39;s Republic of Bulgaria">socialist state</a> and part of the Soviet-led <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a>. The ruling <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Communist_Party" title="Bulgarian Communist Party">Communist Party</a> gave up its monopoly on power after the <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989" title="Revolutions of 1989">Revolutions of 1989</a> and allowed <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party</a> elections. Bulgaria then transitioned into a <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a> and a market-based economy.\n</p><p>Since adopting a democratic constitution in 1991, Bulgaria has been a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a> with a high degree of political, administrative, and economic centralisation. The urbanized population of seven million lives mainly in Sofia and the <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Bulgaria" title="Provinces of Bulgaria">27 provincial capital</a> cities, but faces significant demographic decline. Bulgaria is a member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>; it is a founding state of the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> (OSCE) and has taken a seat at the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">UN Security Council</a> three times. Its <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a> is part of the <a href="/wiki/European_Single_Market" title="European Single Market">European Single Market</a> and mostly relies on services, followed by industry\xe2\x80\x94especially machine building and mining\xe2\x80\x94and agriculture. Widespread corruption continues to be a major socio-economic issue.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#Footnotes"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Footnotes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>\n<p>The name <i>Bulgaria</i> is derived from the <i><a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">Bulgars</a></i>, a tribe of <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic</a> origin that founded the country. Their name is not completely understood and difficult to trace back earlier than the 4th century AD,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGolden1992103\xe2\x80\x93104_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGolden1992103\xe2\x80\x93104-9">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> but it is possibly derived from the <a href="/wiki/Proto-Turkic" class="mw-redirect" title="Proto-Turkic">Proto-Turkic</a> word <i>bul\xc4\xa3ha</i> ("to mix", "shake", "stir") and its derivative <i>bulgak</i> ("revolt", "disorder").<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The meaning may be further extended to "rebel", "incite" or "produce a state of disorder", i.e. the "disturbers".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChen201297_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChen201297-11">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGolden1992104_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGolden1992104-13">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Alternatively, "to mix" or "of mixed stock" is a disputed interpretation of the word referring to the supposed mixing of the <a href="/wiki/Oghur_(tribe)" title="Oghur (tribe)">Oghurs</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">Huns</a> that initiated the Bulgars\' <a href="/wiki/Ethnogenesis" title="Ethnogenesis">ethnogenesis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKaratay200325_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKaratay200325-14">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Such mixing, however, may have occurred earlier. Analogous groups in <a href="/wiki/Inner_Asia" title="Inner Asia">Inner Asia</a> with phonologically similar names were frequently described in similar terms: during the 4th century, the <a href="/wiki/Jie_people" title="Jie people">Buluoji</a>, a component of the "<a href="/wiki/Five_Barbarians" title="Five Barbarians">Five Barbarian</a>" groups in Ancient China, were portrayed as both a "mixed race" and "troublemakers".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChen201292\xe2\x80\x9395,_97_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChen201292\xe2\x80\x9395,_97-15">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Another suggested etymology is related to a nomadic Turkic people known as <a href="/wiki/Onogurs" title="Onogurs">Onogurs</a>, whose name means "ten tribes". Within this theory, <i>Bulgar</i> is a derivation from the Proto-Turkic <i>bel</i> ("five") and <i>gur</i> ("arrow" or "tribe"), indicating a possible <a href="/wiki/Turkic_tribal_confederations" title="Turkic tribal confederations">tribal division</a> within the Onogurs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKaratay200328_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKaratay200328-16">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bulgaria" title="History of Bulgaria">History of Bulgaria</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory_and_antiquity">Prehistory and antiquity</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Europe" title="Neolithic Europe">Neolithic Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Odrysian_kingdom" title="Odrysian kingdom">Odrysian kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thracians" title="Thracians">Thracians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sofia_-_Odrysian_Wreath_from_Golyamata_Mogila.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Thracian golden wreath exhibited in the National Historical Museum" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Sofia_-_Odrysian_Wreath_from_Golyamata_Mogila.jpg/130px-Sofia_-_Odrysian_Wreath_from_Golyamata_Mogila.jpg" width="130" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Sofia_-_Odrysian_Wreath_from_Golyamata_Mogila.jpg/195px-Sofia_-_Odrysian_Wreath_from_Golyamata_Mogila.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Sofia_-_Odrysian_Wreath_from_Golyamata_Mogila.jpg/260px-Sofia_-_Odrysian_Wreath_from_Golyamata_Mogila.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sofia_-_Odrysian_Wreath_from_Golyamata_Mogila.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Odrysian golden <a href="/wiki/Wreath" title="Wreath">wreath</a> in the <a href="/wiki/National_Historical_Museum_(Bulgaria)" title="National Historical Museum (Bulgaria)">National History Museum</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Neanderthal" title="Neanderthal">Neanderthal</a> remains dating to around 150,000 years ago, or the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Paleolithic" title="Middle Paleolithic">Middle Paleolithic</a>, are some of the earliest traces of human activity in the lands of modern Bulgaria.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Crampton1987_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crampton1987-18">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EBHistory_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBHistory-19">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Karanovo_culture" title="Karanovo culture">Karanovo culture</a> arose circa 6,500 BC and was one of several <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> societies in the region that thrived on <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Copper_Age" class="mw-redirect" title="Copper Age">Copper Age</a> <a href="/wiki/Varna_culture" title="Varna culture">Varna culture</a> (fifth millennium BC) is credited with inventing <a href="/wiki/Goldsmith" title="Goldsmith">gold metallurgy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The associated <a href="/wiki/Varna_Necropolis" title="Varna Necropolis">Varna Necropolis treasure</a> contains the oldest golden jewellery in the world with an approximate age of over 6,000 years.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The treasure has been valuable for understanding social hierarchy and stratification in the earliest European societies.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CENTCOM_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CENTCOM-26">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Thracians" title="Thracians">Thracians</a>, one of the three primary ancestral groups of modern Bulgarians, appeared on the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkan Peninsula</a> some time before the 12th century BC.<sup id="cite_ref-Crampton1987_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crampton1987-18">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EBBulgars_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBBulgars-28">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The Thracians excelled in <a href="/wiki/Metallurgy" title="Metallurgy">metallurgy</a> and gave the Greeks the <a href="/wiki/Orpheus" title="Orpheus">Orphean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dionysus" title="Dionysus">Dionysian</a> cults, but remained tribal and stateless.<sup id="cite_ref-EBBalkans_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBBalkans-30">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The Persian <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a> conquered most of present-day Bulgaria in the 6th century BC and retained control over the region until <a href="/wiki/Second_Persian_invasion_of_Greece" title="Second Persian invasion of Greece">479 BC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoismanWorthington2011135\xe2\x80\x93138,_343\xe2\x80\x93345_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoismanWorthington2011135\xe2\x80\x93138,_343\xe2\x80\x93345-32">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The invasion became a catalyst for Thracian unity, and the bulk of their tribes united under king <a href="/wiki/Teres_I" title="Teres I">Teres</a> to form the <a href="/wiki/Odrysian_kingdom" title="Odrysian kingdom">Odrysian kingdom</a> in the 470s BC.<sup id="cite_ref-EBBalkans_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBBalkans-30">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoismanWorthington135\xe2\x80\x93138,_343\xe2\x80\x93345_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoismanWorthington135\xe2\x80\x93138,_343\xe2\x80\x93345-33">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> It was weakened and vassalized by <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Macedon" title="Philip II of Macedon">Philip II of Macedon</a> in 341 BC,<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> attacked <a href="/wiki/Tylis" title="Tylis">by Celts</a> in the 3rd century,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> and finally <a href="/wiki/Thracia" title="Thracia">became a province</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> in 45 AD.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the end of the 1st century AD, Roman governance was established over the entire Balkan Peninsula and <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> began spreading in the region around the 4th century.<sup id="cite_ref-EBBalkans_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBBalkans-30">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Bible" title="Gothic Bible">Gothic Bible</a>\xe2\x80\x94the first <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">Germanic-language</a> book\xe2\x80\x94was created by <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Gothic</a> bishop <a href="/wiki/Ulfilas" title="Ulfilas">Ulfilas</a> in what is today northern Bulgaria around 381.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The region came under <a href="/wiki/Byzantine" class="mw-redirect" title="Byzantine">Byzantine</a> control after the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Western_Roman_Empire" title="Fall of the Western Roman Empire">fall of Rome</a> in 476. However, the Byzantines were engaged in prolonged warfare against Persia and could not defend their Balkan territories from barbarian incursions.<sup id="cite_ref-EBHistory_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBHistory-19">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> This enabled the <a href="/wiki/Early_Slavs" title="Early Slavs">Slavs</a> to enter the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan Peninsula">Balkan Peninsula</a> as marauders, primarily through an area between the Danube River and the Balkan Mountains known as <a href="/wiki/Moesia" title="Moesia">Moesia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Gradually, the interior of the peninsula became a country of the <a href="/wiki/Sclaveni" title="Sclaveni">South Slavs</a>, who lived under a <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The Slavs assimilated the partially <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic_period#Balkans" title="Hellenistic period">Hellenized</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thraco-Romans" class="mw-redirect" title="Thraco-Romans">Romanized</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Thracian_Goths" title="Thracian Goths">Gothicized</a> Thracians in the rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Folk_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Folk-42">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Crampton1987_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crampton1987-18">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_Bulgarian_Empire">First Bulgarian Empire</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">First Bulgarian Empire</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Krum1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Krum feasting with his nobles after the battle of Pliska, detail from the Manasses chronicle" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Krum1.jpg/220px-Krum1.jpg" width="220" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Krum1.jpg/330px-Krum1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Krum1.jpg/440px-Krum1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1689" data-file-height="1296" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Krum1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Khan Krum feasts with his nobles after the battle of Pliska. His servant (far right) brings the wine-filled <a href="/wiki/Skull_cup" title="Skull cup">skull cup</a> of <a href="/wiki/Nicephorus_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Nicephorus I">Nicephorus I</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Not long after the Slavic incursion, Moesia was once again invaded, this time by the <a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">Bulgar</a>s under <a href="/wiki/List_of_Bulgarian_monarchs" title="List of Bulgarian monarchs">Khan</a> <a href="/wiki/Asparuh_of_Bulgaria" title="Asparuh of Bulgaria">Asparukh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Their horde was a remnant of <a href="/wiki/Old_Great_Bulgaria" title="Old Great Bulgaria">Old Great Bulgaria</a>, an extinct tribal confederacy situated north of the Black Sea in what is now Ukraine. Asparukh attacked Byzantine territories in Moesia and conquered the Slavic tribes there in 680.<sup id="cite_ref-EBBulgars_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBBulgars-28">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> A peace treaty with the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> was signed in 681, marking the foundation of the <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">First Bulgarian Empire</a>. The minority Bulgars formed a close-knit ruling caste.<sup id="cite_ref-fine_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fine-47">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Succeeding rulers strengthened the Bulgarian state throughout the 8th and 9th centuries. <a href="/wiki/Krum_of_Bulgaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Krum of Bulgaria">Krum</a> introduced a written code of law<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> and checked a major Byzantine incursion at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Pliska" title="Battle of Pliska">Battle of Pliska</a> where Byzantine emperor <a href="/wiki/Nicephorus_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Nicephorus I">Nicephorus I</a> was killed.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Boris_I_of_Bulgaria" title="Boris I of Bulgaria">Boris I</a> abolished paganism in favour of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Christianity</a> in 864. The <a href="/wiki/Christianization_of_Bulgaria" title="Christianization of Bulgaria">conversion</a> was followed by a Byzantine recognition of the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Orthodox_Church" title="Bulgarian Orthodox Church">Bulgarian church</a><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> and the adoption of the <a href="/wiki/Cyrillic_script" title="Cyrillic script">Cyrillic alphabet</a>, developed in the capital, <a href="/wiki/Preslav" class="mw-redirect" title="Preslav">Preslav</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RCJ_BG_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCJ_BG-51">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The common language, religion and script strengthened central authority and gradually fused the Slavs and Bulgars into a unified people speaking a single <a href="/wiki/Slavic_languages" title="Slavic languages">Slavic</a> language.<sup id="cite_ref-EBBulgars_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBBulgars-28">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EB_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-52">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RCJ_BG_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCJ_BG-51">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> A cultural golden age began during the 34-year rule of <a href="/wiki/Simeon_I_of_Bulgaria" title="Simeon I of Bulgaria">Simeon the Great</a>, who also oversaw the largest territorial expansion of the state.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_First_Golden_Age_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_First_Golden_Age-53">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After Simeon\'s death, Bulgaria was weakened by wars with <a href="/wiki/Magyars" class="mw-redirect" title="Magyars">Magyars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pechenegs" title="Pechenegs">Pechenegs</a> and the spread of the <a href="/wiki/Bogomilism" title="Bogomilism">Bogomil heresy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-52">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Preslav was seized by the Byzantine army in 971 after consecutive <a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus&#39;">Rus\'</a> and Byzantine invasions.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_52-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-52">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The empire briefly recovered from the attacks under <a href="/wiki/Samuel_of_Bulgaria" title="Samuel of Bulgaria">Samuil</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> but this ended when Byzantine emperor <a href="/wiki/Basil_II" title="Basil II">Basil II</a> defeated the Bulgarian army at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kleidion" title="Battle of Kleidion">Klyuch</a> in 1014. Samuil died shortly after the battle,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> and by 1018 the Byzantines <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_conquest_of_Bulgaria" title="Byzantine conquest of Bulgaria">had ended the First Bulgarian Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_Bulgarian_Empire">Second Bulgarian Empire</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Second_Bulgarian_Empire" title="Second Bulgarian Empire">Second Bulgarian Empire</a></div>\n<p>After the conquest of Bulgaria, Basil II prevented revolts by retaining the rule of local nobility and relieving their lands of the obligation to pay taxes in gold, allowing <a href="/wiki/Tax_in_kind" title="Tax in kind">tax in kind</a> instead.<sup id="cite_ref-Ostrog_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ostrog-58">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Orthodox_Church" title="Bulgarian Orthodox Church">Bulgarian Patriarchate</a> was reduced to an <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Archbishopric_of_Ohrid_(ancient)" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Archbishopric of Ohrid (ancient)">archbishopric</a>, but retained its <a href="/wiki/Autocephaly" title="Autocephaly">autocephalous status</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Diocese" title="Diocese">dioceses</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ostrog_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ostrog-58">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Byzantine domestic policies changed after Basil\'s death and a series of unsuccessful rebellions broke out, <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_uprising_against_the_Byzantine_Empire_(1040-1041)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulgarian uprising against the Byzantine Empire (1040-1041)">the largest</a> being led by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Delyan" title="Peter Delyan">Peter Delyan</a>. In 1185 <a href="/wiki/Asen_dynasty" title="Asen dynasty">Asen dynasty</a> nobles <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Asen_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Ivan Asen I">Ivan Asen I</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peter_IV_of_Bulgaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Peter IV of Bulgaria">Peter IV</a> organized a <a href="/wiki/Uprising_of_Asen_and_Peter" title="Uprising of Asen and Peter">major uprising</a> which resulted in the re-establishment of the Bulgarian state. Ivan Asen and Peter laid the foundations of the Second Bulgarian Empire with <a href="/wiki/Veliko_Tarnovo" title="Veliko Tarnovo">Tarnovo</a> as the capital.<sup id="cite_ref-EBSecondEmpire_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBSecondEmpire-60">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20140621_Veliko_Tarnovo_002.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A view of the walls of Tsarevets fortress in Tarnovo" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/20140621_Veliko_Tarnovo_002.jpg/220px-20140621_Veliko_Tarnovo_002.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/20140621_Veliko_Tarnovo_002.jpg/330px-20140621_Veliko_Tarnovo_002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/20140621_Veliko_Tarnovo_002.jpg/440px-20140621_Veliko_Tarnovo_002.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3243" data-file-height="1821" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20140621_Veliko_Tarnovo_002.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The walls of <a href="/wiki/Tsarevets_(fortress)" title="Tsarevets (fortress)">Tsarevets fortress</a> in <a href="/wiki/Veliko_Tarnovo" title="Veliko Tarnovo">Veliko Tarnovo</a>, the capital of the second empire</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Kaloyan" class="mw-redirect" title="Kaloyan">Kaloyan</a>, the third of the Asen monarchs, extended his dominion to <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ohrid" title="Ohrid">Ohrid</a>. He acknowledged the spiritual supremacy of <a href="/wiki/The_pope" class="mw-redirect" title="The pope">the pope</a> and received a royal crown from a <a href="/wiki/Papal_legate" title="Papal legate">papal legate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EB1911_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB1911-61">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The empire reached its zenith under <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Asen_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Ivan Asen II">Ivan Asen II</a> (1218\xe2\x80\x931241), when its borders expanded as far as the coast of <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, Serbia and <a href="/wiki/Epirus" title="Epirus">Epirus</a>, while commerce and culture flourished.<sup id="cite_ref-EB1911_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB1911-61">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EBSecondEmpire_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBSecondEmpire-60">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Ivan Asen\'s rule was also marked by a shift away from Rome in religious matters.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Asen dynasty became extinct in 1257. Internal conflicts and incessant Byzantine and Hungarian attacks followed, enabling the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Mongols</a> to <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Bulgaria_and_Serbia" title="Mongol invasion of Bulgaria and Serbia">establish suzerainty</a> over the weakened Bulgarian state.<sup id="cite_ref-EB1911_61-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB1911-61">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> In 1277, swineherd <a href="/wiki/Ivaylo_of_Bulgaria" title="Ivaylo of Bulgaria">Ivaylo</a> led a <a href="/wiki/Uprising_of_Ivaylo" title="Uprising of Ivaylo">great peasant revolt</a> that chased the Mongols out of Bulgaria and briefly made him emperor.<sup id="cite_ref-Martin_2017_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martin_2017-64">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EBSecondEmpire_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBSecondEmpire-60">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> He was overthrown in 1280 by <a href="/wiki/Boyars" class="mw-redirect" title="Boyars">the feudal landlords</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Martin_2017_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martin_2017-64">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> whose factional conflicts caused the Second Bulgarian Empire to disintegrate into small feudal dominions by the 14th century.<sup id="cite_ref-EBSecondEmpire_60-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBSecondEmpire-60">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> These fragmented <a href="/wiki/Rump_state" title="Rump state">rump states</a>\xe2\x80\x94two tsardoms at <a href="/wiki/Tsardom_of_Vidin" title="Tsardom of Vidin">Vidin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Bulgarian_Empire#Ivan_Alexander_and_fall_of_Bulgaria" title="Second Bulgarian Empire">Tarnovo</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Despotate_of_Dobruja" title="Despotate of Dobruja">Despotate of Dobrudzha</a>\xe2\x80\x94became easy prey for a new threat arriving from the Southeast: the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turks" title="Ottoman Turks">Ottoman Turks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EB1911_61-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB1911-61">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ottoman_rule">Ottoman rule</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Bulgaria" title="Ottoman Bulgaria">Ottoman Bulgaria</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bulgaria_Ivan_Alexander_(1331-1371).svg" class="image"><img alt="Map of the 14th century Bulgarian rump states" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Bulgaria_Ivan_Alexander_%281331-1371%29.svg/220px-Bulgaria_Ivan_Alexander_%281331-1371%29.svg.png" width="220" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Bulgaria_Ivan_Alexander_%281331-1371%29.svg/330px-Bulgaria_Ivan_Alexander_%281331-1371%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Bulgaria_Ivan_Alexander_%281331-1371%29.svg/440px-Bulgaria_Ivan_Alexander_%281331-1371%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="391" data-file-height="319" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bulgaria_Ivan_Alexander_(1331-1371).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fragmentation of the Second Bulgarian Empire in the 14th century</div></div></div>\n<p>The Ottomans were employed as mercenaries by the Byzantines in the 1340s but later became invaders in their own right.<sup id="cite_ref-Ottoman_rule_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ottoman_rule-65">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Sultan <a href="/wiki/Murad_I" title="Murad I">Murad I</a> took <a href="/wiki/Adrianople" class="mw-redirect" title="Adrianople">Adrianople</a> from the Byzantines in 1362; <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a> fell in 1382, followed by <a href="/wiki/Shumen" title="Shumen">Shumen</a> in 1388.<sup id="cite_ref-Ottoman_rule_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ottoman_rule-65">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The Ottomans completed their conquest of Bulgarian lands in 1393 when Tarnovo was sacked after a three-month siege, and then the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nicopolis" title="Battle of Nicopolis">Battle of Nicopolis</a> which brought about the fall of the Vidin Tsardom in 1396. The Bulgarian nobility was subsequently eliminated and the peasantry was <a href="/wiki/Serfdom" title="Serfdom">enserfed</a> to Ottoman masters,<sup id="cite_ref-Ottoman_rule_65-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ottoman_rule-65">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> while much of the educated clergy fled to other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Jire\xc4\x8dek_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jire\xc4\x8dek-66">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Christians were considered an <a href="/wiki/Rayah" title="Rayah">inferior class</a> of people under the Ottoman system. Bulgarians were subjected to heavy taxes (including <a href="/wiki/Devshirme" title="Devshirme">devshirme</a>, or <i>blood tax</i>), their culture was suppressed,<sup id="cite_ref-Jire\xc4\x8dek_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jire\xc4\x8dek-66">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> and they experienced partial <a href="/wiki/Islamisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamisation">Islamisation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Ottoman authorities established a religious administrative community called the Rum <a href="/wiki/Millet_(Ottoman_Empire)" title="Millet (Ottoman Empire)">Millet</a>, which governed all Orthodox Christians regardless of their ethnicity.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Most of the local population then gradually lost its distinct national consciousness, identifying only by its faith.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> However, the clergy remaining in some isolated monasteries kept their ethnic identity alive, enabling its survival in remote rural areas,<sup id="cite_ref-Crampton1987_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crampton1987-18">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> and in the militant <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Bulgaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Bulgaria">Catholic community</a> in the northwest of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As Ottoman power began to wane, <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Habsburg Austria</a> and Russia saw Bulgarian Christians as potential allies. The Austrians first backed an <a href="/wiki/First_Tarnovo_Uprising" title="First Tarnovo Uprising">uprising in Tarnovo in 1598</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Second_Tarnovo_Uprising" title="Second Tarnovo Uprising">a second one in 1686</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Chiprovtsi_Uprising" class="mw-redirect" title="Chiprovtsi Uprising">Chiprovtsi Uprising</a> in 1688 and finally <a href="/wiki/Karposh%27s_Rebellion" class="mw-redirect" title="Karposh&#39;s Rebellion">Karposh\'s Rebellion</a> in 1689.<sup id="cite_ref-Decline_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Decline-72">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> also asserted itself as a protector of Christians in Ottoman lands with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_K%C3%BC%C3%A7%C3%BCk_Kaynarca" title="Treaty of K\xc3\xbc\xc3\xa7\xc3\xbck Kaynarca">Treaty of K\xc3\xbc\xc3\xa7\xc3\xbck Kaynarca</a> in 1774.<sup id="cite_ref-Decline_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Decline-72">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_defeat_of_Shipka_Peak,_Bulgarian_War_of_Independence.JPG" class="image"><img alt="The Defence of the Eagle&#39;s Nest, painting by Alexey Popov from 1893, depicting the Defence of Shipka Pass" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/The_defeat_of_Shipka_Peak%2C_Bulgarian_War_of_Independence.JPG/220px-The_defeat_of_Shipka_Peak%2C_Bulgarian_War_of_Independence.JPG" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/The_defeat_of_Shipka_Peak%2C_Bulgarian_War_of_Independence.JPG/330px-The_defeat_of_Shipka_Peak%2C_Bulgarian_War_of_Independence.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/The_defeat_of_Shipka_Peak%2C_Bulgarian_War_of_Independence.JPG/440px-The_defeat_of_Shipka_Peak%2C_Bulgarian_War_of_Independence.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1134" data-file-height="827" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_defeat_of_Shipka_Peak,_Bulgarian_War_of_Independence.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Russo-Bulgarian defence of Shipka Pass</div></div></div>\n<p>The Western European <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Enlightenment</a> in the 18th century influenced the initiation of a <a href="/wiki/National_awakening_of_Bulgaria" title="National awakening of Bulgaria">national awakening of Bulgaria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ottoman_rule_65-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ottoman_rule-65">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> It restored national consciousness and provided an ideological basis for the liberation struggle, resulting in the 1876 <a href="/wiki/April_Uprising" class="mw-redirect" title="April Uprising">April Uprising</a>. Up to 30,000 Bulgarians were killed as Ottoman authorities put down the rebellion. The massacres prompted the <a href="/wiki/Great_Powers#History" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Powers">Great Powers</a> to take action.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Final_Move_to_Independence_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Final_Move_to_Independence-73">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> They convened the <a href="/wiki/Constantinople_Conference" title="Constantinople Conference">Constantinople Conference</a> in 1876, but their decisions were rejected by the Ottomans. This allowed the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> to seek a military solution without risking confrontation with other Great Powers, as had happened in the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Final_Move_to_Independence_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Final_Move_to_Independence-73">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In 1877 <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War,_1877%E2%80%931878" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Turkish War, 1877\xe2\x80\x931878">Russia declared war</a> on the Ottomans and defeated them with the help of <a href="/wiki/Opalchentsi" class="mw-redirect" title="Opalchentsi">Bulgarian rebels</a>, particularly during the crucial <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Shipka_Pass" title="Battle of Shipka Pass">Battle of Shipka Pass</a> which secured Russian control over the main road to <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Third_Bulgarian_state">Third Bulgarian state</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bulgaria_(1878%E2%80%931946)" title="History of Bulgaria (1878\xe2\x80\x931946)">History of Bulgaria (1878\xe2\x80\x931946)</a>, <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Bulgaria" title="People&#39;s Republic of Bulgaria">People\'s Republic of Bulgaria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bulgaria_since_1989" title="History of Bulgaria since 1989">History of Bulgaria since 1989</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_San_Stefano" title="Treaty of San Stefano">Treaty of San Stefano</a> was signed on 3 March 1878 by Russia and the Ottoman Empire. It was to set up an autonomous Bulgarian principality spanning Moesia, <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(region)" title="Macedonia (region)">Macedonia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thrace" title="Thrace">Thrace</a>, roughly on the territories of the Second Bulgarian Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESan_Stefano,_Berlin_and_Independence_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESan_Stefano,_Berlin_and_Independence-76">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The other <a href="/wiki/Great_Powers#History" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Powers">Great Powers</a> immediately rejected the treaty out of fear that such a large country in the Balkans might threaten their interests. It was superseded by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Berlin,_1878" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Berlin, 1878">Treaty of Berlin</a>, signed on 13 July, which provided for a much smaller state only comprising Moesia and the region of <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a>, leaving large populations of ethnic Bulgarians outside the new country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESan_Stefano,_Berlin_and_Independence_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESan_Stefano,_Berlin_and_Independence-76">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBCProfile_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCProfile-78">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> This significantly contributed to Bulgaria\'s militaristic foreign affairs approach during the first half of the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistorical_Setting_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistorical_Setting-79">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Bulgarian principality won <a href="/wiki/Serbo-Bulgarian_War" title="Serbo-Bulgarian War">a war against Serbia</a> and incorporated the semi-autonomous Ottoman territory of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Rumelia" title="Eastern Rumelia">Eastern Rumelia</a> in 1885, proclaiming itself an independent state on 5 October 1908.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> In the years following independence, Bulgaria increasingly militarized and was often referred to as "the Balkan <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> It became involved in three consecutive conflicts between 1912 and 1918\xe2\x80\x94two <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Wars" title="Balkan Wars">Balkan Wars</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. After a disastrous defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Balkan_War" title="Second Balkan War">Second Balkan War</a>, Bulgaria again found itself fighting on the losing side as a result of its alliance with the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a> in World War I. Despite fielding more than a quarter of its population in a 1,200,000-strong army<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> and achieving several decisive victories at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Doiran_(1917)" title="Battle of Doiran (1917)">Doiran</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Monastir_(1917)" title="Battle of Monastir (1917)">Monastir</a>, the country capitulated in 1918. The war resulted in significant territorial losses and a total of 87,500 soldiers killed.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> More than 253,000 refugees from the lost territories <a href="/wiki/Immigrated" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigrated">immigrated</a> to Bulgaria from 1912 to 1929,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> placing additional strain on the already ruined national economy.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BASA-3K-7-342-28-Boris_III_of_Bulgaria.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="A portrait of Tsar Boris III" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/BASA-3K-7-342-28-Boris_III_of_Bulgaria.jpeg/150px-BASA-3K-7-342-28-Boris_III_of_Bulgaria.jpeg" width="150" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/BASA-3K-7-342-28-Boris_III_of_Bulgaria.jpeg/225px-BASA-3K-7-342-28-Boris_III_of_Bulgaria.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/BASA-3K-7-342-28-Boris_III_of_Bulgaria.jpeg/300px-BASA-3K-7-342-28-Boris_III_of_Bulgaria.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1911" data-file-height="2543" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BASA-3K-7-342-28-Boris_III_of_Bulgaria.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tsar Boris III</div></div></div>\n<p>The resulting political unrest led to the establishment of a royal <a href="/wiki/Authoritarianism" title="Authoritarianism">authoritarian dictatorship</a> by Tsar <a href="/wiki/Boris_III_of_Bulgaria" title="Boris III of Bulgaria">Boris III</a> (1918\xe2\x80\x931943). Bulgaria entered World War II in 1941 as a member of <a href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" class="mw-redirect" title="Axis Powers">the Axis</a> but declined to participate in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">Operation Barbarossa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rescue_of_the_Bulgarian_Jews" title="Rescue of the Bulgarian Jews">saved its Jewish population</a> from deportation to <a href="/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camps" title="Nazi concentration camps">concentration camps</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBulgaria_in_World_War_II:_The_Passive_Alliance_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBulgaria_in_World_War_II:_The_Passive_Alliance-87">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The sudden death of Boris III in the summer of 1943 pushed the country into political turmoil as the war turned against Germany, and the communist guerrilla movement gained momentum. The government of <a href="/wiki/Bogdan_Filov" title="Bogdan Filov">Bogdan Filov</a> subsequently failed to achieve peace with the Allies. Bulgaria did not comply with Soviet demands to expel German forces from its territory, resulting in a declaration of war and an invasion by the USSR in September 1944.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWartime_Crisis_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWartime_Crisis-88">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> The communist-dominated <a href="/wiki/Fatherland_Front_(Bulgaria)" title="Fatherland Front (Bulgaria)">Fatherland Front</a> took power, ended participation in the Axis and joined the Allied side until the war ended.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Bulgaria suffered little war damage and the Soviet Union demanded no reparations. But all wartime gains, with the notable exception of <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Craiova" title="Treaty of Craiova">Southern Dobrudzha</a>, were lost.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Soviet_Occupation_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Soviet_Occupation-90">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_of_1944" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulgarian coup d&#39;\xc3\xa9tat of 1944">left-wing uprising</a> of 9 September 1944 led to the abolition of monarchic rule and <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Court_(Bulgaria)" title="People&#39;s Court (Bulgaria)">the executions</a> of some 1,000\xe2\x80\x943,000 dissidents, war criminals, and members of the former royal elite.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> But it was not until 1946 that a <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">one-party</a> <a href="/wiki/People%27s_republic" class="mw-redirect" title="People&#39;s republic">people\'s republic</a> was instituted following a referendum.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> It fell into the Soviet sphere of influence under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Georgi_Dimitrov" title="Georgi Dimitrov">Georgi Dimitrov</a> (1946\xe2\x80\x931949), who established a repressive, rapidly industrializing <a href="/wiki/Stalinism" title="Stalinism">Stalinist</a> state.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Soviet_Occupation_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Soviet_Occupation-90">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> By the mid-1950s standards of living rose significantly and political repressions eased.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDomestic_Policy_and_Its_Results_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDomestic_Policy_and_Its_Results-95">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAfter_Stalin_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAfter_Stalin-96">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> The Soviet-style <a href="/wiki/Planned_economy" title="Planned economy">planned economy</a> saw some market-oriented policies emerging on an experimental level under <a href="/wiki/Todor_Zhivkov" title="Todor Zhivkov">Todor Zhivkov</a> (1954\xe2\x80\x931989).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Economy_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Economy-97">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Compared to wartime levels, national GDP increased five-fold and per capita GDP quadrupled by the 1980s,<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> although severe debt spikes took place in 1960, 1977 and 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Zhivkov\'s daughter <a href="/wiki/Lyudmila_Zhivkova" title="Lyudmila Zhivkova">Lyudmila</a> bolstered national pride by promoting Bulgarian heritage, culture and arts worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Political_Atmosphere_in_the_1970s_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Political_Atmosphere_in_the_1970s-100">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Facing declining birth rates among the ethnic Bulgarian majority, in 1984 Zhivkov\'s government forced the minority <a href="/wiki/Turks_in_Bulgaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Turks in Bulgaria">ethnic Turks</a> to adopt Slavic names in an attempt to erase their identity and assimilate them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBulgaria_in_the_1980s_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBulgaria_in_the_1980s-101">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> These policies resulted in the emigration of some 300,000 ethnic Turks to Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Communist Party was forced to give up its political monopoly on 10 November 1989 under the influence of the <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989" title="Revolutions of 1989">Revolutions of 1989</a>. Zhivkov resigned and Bulgaria embarked on a transition to a parliamentary democracy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGovernment_and_Politics_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGovernment_and_Politics-104">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The first free elections in June 1990 were won by the Communist Party, now rebranded as the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Socialist_Party" title="Bulgarian Socialist Party">Bulgarian Socialist Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bulgaria" title="Constitution of Bulgaria">new constitution</a> that provided for a relatively weak elected president and for a prime minister accountable to the legislature was adopted in July 1991. The new system initially failed to improve living standards or create economic growth\xe2\x80\x94the average quality of life and economic performance remained lower than under communism well into the early 2000s.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> A 1997 reform package restored economic growth, but living standards continued to suffer.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> After 2001 economic, political and geopolitical conditions improved greatly,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200616_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200616-108">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> and Bulgaria achieved high Human Development status in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> It became a member of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> in 2004<sup id="cite_ref-nato_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nato-110">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> and participated in the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001\xe2\x80\x93present)">War in Afghanistan</a>. After several years of reforms it joined the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Single_Market" title="European Single Market">single market</a> in 2007 despite Brussels\' concerns about government corruption.<sup id="cite_ref-Ind_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ind-111">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Bulgaria hosted the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_the_Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Presidency of the Council of the European Union">Presidency of the Council of the European Union</a> at the National Palace of Culture in Sofia.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Bulgaria" title="Geography of Bulgaria">Geography of Bulgaria</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bulgaria-geographic_map-en.svg" class="image"><img alt="Topographic map of Bulgaria" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Bulgaria-geographic_map-en.svg/260px-Bulgaria-geographic_map-en.svg.png" width="260" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Bulgaria-geographic_map-en.svg/390px-Bulgaria-geographic_map-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Bulgaria-geographic_map-en.svg/520px-Bulgaria-geographic_map-en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2483" data-file-height="1642" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bulgaria-geographic_map-en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of Bulgaria showing its main topographical features</div></div></div>\n<p>Bulgaria occupies a portion of the eastern <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkan</a> peninsula, bordering five countries\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(country)" class="mw-redirect" title="Macedonia (country)">Macedonia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> to the west, and <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> to the north. The land borders have a total length of 1,808 kilometres (1,123&#160;mi), and the coastline has a length of 354 kilometres (220&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress20064_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress20064-113">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Its total area of 110,994 square kilometres (42,855&#160;sq&#160;mi) ranks it as the world\'s 105th-largest country.<sup id="cite_ref-Penin_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Penin-4">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Bulgaria\'s geographic coordinates are <a href="/wiki/43rd_parallel_north" title="43rd parallel north">43\xc2\xb0 N</a> <a href="/wiki/25th_meridian_east" title="25th meridian east">25\xc2\xb0 E</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook-115">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> The most notable <a href="/wiki/Topographical" class="mw-redirect" title="Topographical">topographical</a> features are the <a href="/wiki/Danubian_Plain_(Bulgaria)" title="Danubian Plain (Bulgaria)">Danubian Plain</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Mountains" title="Balkan Mountains">Balkan Mountains</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Thracian_Plain" class="mw-redirect" title="Thracian Plain">Thracian Plain</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Rhodope_Mountains" title="Rhodope Mountains">Rhodope Mountains</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress20064_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress20064-113">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> The southern edge of the Danubian Plain slopes upward into the foothills of the Balkans, while the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> defines the border with Romania. The <a href="/wiki/Thracia" title="Thracia">Thracian</a> Plain is roughly triangular, beginning southeast of <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a> and broadening as it reaches the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Black_Sea_Coast" title="Bulgarian Black Sea Coast">Black Sea coast</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress20064_113-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress20064-113">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pirin-mountains-Bansko.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A view of snowy Pirin Mountain" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Pirin-mountains-Bansko.jpg/220px-Pirin-mountains-Bansko.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Pirin-mountains-Bansko.jpg/330px-Pirin-mountains-Bansko.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Pirin-mountains-Bansko.jpg/440px-Pirin-mountains-Bansko.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pirin-mountains-Bansko.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pirin Mountain in the southwest</div></div></div>\n<p>The Balkan mountains run laterally through the middle of the country. The mountainous southwest has two distinct alpine ranges\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/Rila" title="Rila">Rila</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pirin" title="Pirin">Pirin</a>, which border the lower but more extensive <a href="/wiki/Rhodope_Mountains" title="Rhodope Mountains">Rhodope Mountains</a> to the east.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress20064_113-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress20064-113">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Musala" title="Musala">Musala</a> peak, at 2,925 metres (9,596&#160;ft), is the highest point in both Bulgaria and the Balkan peninsula, and the Black Sea coast is the country\'s lowest point.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook-115">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Plains occupy about one-third of the territory, while plateaus and hills occupy 41 per cent.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETopography_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETopography-116">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Most rivers are short and with low water levels. The longest river located solely in Bulgarian territory, the <a href="/wiki/Iskar_(river)" title="Iskar (river)">Iskar</a>, has a length of 368 kilometres (229&#160;mi). Other major rivers include the <a href="/wiki/Struma_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Struma River">Struma</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Maritsa" title="Maritsa">Maritsa</a> in the south.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENSI_Brochure20182-3_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENSI_Brochure20182-3-117">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress20064_113-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress20064-113">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bulgaria has a changeable climate, which results from being positioned at the meeting point of the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a> and continental air masses combined with the barrier effect of its mountains.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress20064_113-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress20064-113">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Northern Bulgaria averages 1&#160;\xc2\xb0C (1.8&#160;\xc2\xb0F) cooler, and registers 200 millimetres (7.9&#160;in) more precipitation, than the regions south of the Balkan mountains. Temperature amplitudes vary significantly in different areas. The lowest recorded temperature is \xe2\x88\x9238.3&#160;\xc2\xb0C (\xe2\x88\x9236.9&#160;\xc2\xb0F), while the highest is 45.2&#160;\xc2\xb0C (113.4&#160;\xc2\xb0F).<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">Precipitation</a> averages about 630 millimetres (24.8&#160;in) per year, and varies from 500 millimetres (19.7&#160;in) in <a href="/wiki/Dobrudja" class="mw-redirect" title="Dobrudja">Dobrudja</a> to more than 2,500 millimetres (98.4&#160;in) in the mountains. Continental air masses bring significant amounts of snowfall during winter.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClimate_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClimate-119">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity_and_environment">Biodiversity and environment</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lacerta_viridis_%D0%97%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD_%D0%B3%D1%83%D1%89%D0%B5%D1%80.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A Lacerta viridis, or European green lizard, atop a tree stump in the Ropotamo reserve" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Lacerta_viridis_%D0%97%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD_%D0%B3%D1%83%D1%89%D0%B5%D1%80.jpg/220px-Lacerta_viridis_%D0%97%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD_%D0%B3%D1%83%D1%89%D0%B5%D1%80.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Lacerta_viridis_%D0%97%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD_%D0%B3%D1%83%D1%89%D0%B5%D1%80.jpg/330px-Lacerta_viridis_%D0%97%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD_%D0%B3%D1%83%D1%89%D0%B5%D1%80.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Lacerta_viridis_%D0%97%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD_%D0%B3%D1%83%D1%89%D0%B5%D1%80.jpg/440px-Lacerta_viridis_%D0%97%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD_%D0%B3%D1%83%D1%89%D0%B5%D1%80.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3600" data-file-height="2400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lacerta_viridis_%D0%97%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD_%D0%B3%D1%83%D1%89%D0%B5%D1%80.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Lacerta_viridis" class="mw-redirect" title="Lacerta viridis">Lacerta viridis</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Ropotamo" title="Ropotamo">Ropotamo</a>, one of Bulgaria\'s 16 biosphere reserves</div></div></div>\n<p>The interaction of climatic, hydrological, geological and topographical conditions has produced a relatively wide variety of plant and animal species.<sup id="cite_ref-biodiversity_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biodiversity-120">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\nBulgaria\'s <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>, one of the richest in Europe,<sup id="cite_ref-diversity_of_flora_and_fauna_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity_of_flora_and_fauna-121">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> \n<a href="/wiki/List_of_protected_areas_of_Bulgaria" title="List of protected areas of Bulgaria">is conserved</a> in three national parks, 11 nature parks, 16 <a href="/wiki/Biosphere_reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="Biosphere reserve">biosphere reserves</a> and 565 protected areas.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENSI_Brochure201829_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENSI_Brochure201829-122">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Ninety-three of the 233 <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">mammal</a> species of Europe are found in Bulgaria, along with 49 per cent of <a href="/wiki/Butterfly" title="Butterfly">butterfly</a> and 30 per cent of <a href="/wiki/Vascular_plant" title="Vascular plant">vascular plant</a> species.<sup id="cite_ref-IUCN_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IUCN-125">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Overall, 41,493 plant and animal species are present.<sup id="cite_ref-IUCN_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IUCN-125">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Larger mammals with sizable populations include <a href="/wiki/Deer" title="Deer">deer</a> (106,323 individuals), <a href="/wiki/Wild_boar" title="Wild boar">wild boars</a> (88,948), <a href="/wiki/Jackal" title="Jackal">jackals</a> (47,293) and <a href="/wiki/Fox" title="Fox">foxes</a> (32,326). <a href="/wiki/Partridge" title="Partridge">Partridges</a> number some 328,000 individuals, making them the most widespread <a href="/wiki/Game_(hunting)" title="Game (hunting)">gamebird</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENSI_Brochure20183_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENSI_Brochure20183-126">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> A third of all nesting birds in Bulgaria can be found in <a href="/wiki/Rila_National_Park" title="Rila National Park">Rila National Park</a>, which also hosts Arctic and alpine species at high altitudes.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_Bio_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB_Bio-127">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Flora includes more than 3,800 vascular plant species of which 170 are <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a> and 150 are considered endangered.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> A checklist of larger <a href="/wiki/Fungi" class="mw-redirect" title="Fungi">fungi</a> in Bulgaria by the Institute of Botany identifies more than 1,500 species.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> More than 35 per cent of the land area is covered by forests.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>In 1998, the Bulgarian government adopted the National Biological Diversity Conservation Strategy, a comprehensive programme seeking the preservation of local ecosystems, protection of endangered species and conservation of genetic resources.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Bulgaria has some of the largest <a href="/wiki/Natura_2000" title="Natura 2000">Natura 2000</a> areas in Europe covering 33.8 per cent of its territory.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> It also adopted the <a href="/wiki/Kyoto_Protocol" title="Kyoto Protocol">Kyoto Protocol</a> and achieved its objective of reducing <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_emissions" class="mw-redirect" title="Carbon dioxide emissions">carbon dioxide emissions</a> by 30 per cent from 1990 to 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Bulgaria ranks 30th in the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Performance_Index" title="Environmental Performance Index">Environmental Performance Index</a>, but scores low on air quality.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>Pollution from factories and metallurgy works, and severe <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a>, continue to cause major problems for the health and welfare of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Particulates" title="Particulates">Particulate matter</a> levels are the highest in Europe,<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> especially in urban areas affected by automobile traffic and coal-based power stations.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> One of these, the <a href="/wiki/Lignite" title="Lignite">lignite</a>-fired <a href="/wiki/Maritsa_Iztok_Complex" title="Maritsa Iztok Complex">Maritsa Iztok-2</a> station, is causing the highest damage to <a href="/wiki/Health" title="Health">health</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Environmental_degradation" title="Environmental degradation">environment</a> in the European Union.<sup id="cite_ref-EEA_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EEA-140">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Pesticide usage in agriculture, and antiquated industrial sewage systems, produce extensive soil and water pollution from chemicals and <a href="/wiki/Detergents" class="mw-redirect" title="Detergents">detergents</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ESI_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESI-141">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> An improvement of water quality began in 1998 and has maintained a sustainable trend of moderate improvement. Over 75 per cent of surface rivers meet the standards for good quality.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Bulgaria" title="Politics of Bulgaria">Politics of Bulgaria</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:National_Assembly_of_Bulgaria.jpg" class="image"><img alt="The National Assembly building in Sofia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/National_Assembly_of_Bulgaria.jpg/220px-National_Assembly_of_Bulgaria.jpg" width="220" height="107" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/National_Assembly_of_Bulgaria.jpg/330px-National_Assembly_of_Bulgaria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/National_Assembly_of_Bulgaria.jpg/440px-National_Assembly_of_Bulgaria.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3298" data-file-height="1600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:National_Assembly_of_Bulgaria.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The National Assembly in <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Bulgaria is a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_democracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary democracy">parliamentary democracy</a> where the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Bulgaria" title="Prime Minister of Bulgaria">prime minister</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> and the most powerful executive position.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200616_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200616-108">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> The political system has three branches\xe2\x80\x94legislative, executive and judicial, with <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a> for <a href="/wiki/Citizen" class="mw-redirect" title="Citizen">citizens</a> at least 18 years old. The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bulgaria" title="Constitution of Bulgaria">Constitution</a> also provides possibilities of direct democracy, namely petitions and national <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referenda</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DD-Navi_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DD-Navi-143">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> Elections are supervised by an independent Central Election Commission that includes members from all major political parties. Parties must register with the commission prior to participating in a national election.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200617_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200617-144">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> Normally, the prime minister-elect is the leader of the party receiving the most votes in parliamentary elections, although this is not always the case.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200616_108-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200616-108">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Unlike the prime minister, presidential domestic power is more limited. The directly elected <a href="/wiki/President_of_Bulgaria" title="President of Bulgaria">President</a> serves as <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a> of the armed forces, and has the authority to return a bill for further debate, although the parliament can override the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_veto" class="mw-redirect" title="Presidential veto">presidential veto</a> by a simple majority vote.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200616_108-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200616-108">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Political parties gather in the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Bulgaria)" title="National Assembly (Bulgaria)">National Assembly</a>, a body of 240 deputies elected to four-year terms by direct popular vote. The National Assembly has the power to enact laws, approve the budget, schedule presidential elections, select and dismiss the prime minister and other ministers, declare war, deploy troops abroad, and ratify international treaties and agreements.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200616-17_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200616-17-145">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:286px;max-width:286px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Rumen_Radev.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Portrait of president Rumen Radev" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Rumen_Radev.jpg/150px-Rumen_Radev.jpg" width="150" height="167" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Rumen_Radev.jpg/225px-Rumen_Radev.jpg 1.5x,
