Vocal Choir</a> won a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> in 1990 for its performances of Bulgarian folk music.<sup id="cite_ref-349" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-349">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup> Written musical composition can be traced back to the works of <a href="/wiki/Yoan_Kukuzel" class="mw-redirect" title="Yoan Kukuzel">Yoan Kukuzel</a> (c. 1280\xe2\x80\x931360),<sup id="cite_ref-350" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-350">&#91;347&#93;</a></sup> but modern classical music began with <a href="/wiki/Emanuil_Manolov" title="Emanuil Manolov">Emanuil Manolov</a>, who composed the first Bulgarian <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">opera</a> in 1890.<sup id="cite_ref-Cultural_life_335-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cultural_life-335">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pancho_Vladigerov" title="Pancho Vladigerov">Pancho Vladigerov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Petko_Staynov" title="Petko Staynov">Petko Staynov</a> further enriched <a href="/wiki/Symphony" title="Symphony">symphony</a>, ballet and opera, which singers <a href="/wiki/Ghena_Dimitrova" title="Ghena Dimitrova">Ghena Dimitrova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boris_Christoff" title="Boris Christoff">Boris Hristov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nicolai_Ghiaurov" title="Nicolai Ghiaurov">Nikolay Gyaurov</a> elevated to a world-class level.<sup id="cite_ref-Cultural_life_335-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cultural_life-335">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">&#91;348&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-352" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-352">&#91;349&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-353">&#91;350&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-354" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-354">&#91;351&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-355">&#91;352&#93;</a></sup> Bulgarian performers have also gained acclaim in other genres like <a href="/wiki/Electropop" title="Electropop">electropop</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mira_Aroyo" title="Mira Aroyo">Mira Aroyo</a>), <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a> (<a href="/wiki/Milcho_Leviev" title="Milcho Leviev">Milcho Leviev</a>) and blends of jazz and folk (<a href="/wiki/Ivo_Papazov" title="Ivo Papazov">Ivo Papazov</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Cultural_life_335-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cultural_life-335">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cultural events are advertized in the largest media outlets, including the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_National_Radio" title="Bulgarian National Radio">Bulgarian National Radio</a>, and daily newspapers <i><a href="/wiki/Trud_(Bulgarian_newspaper)" title="Trud (Bulgarian newspaper)">Trud</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dnevnik_(Bulgaria)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dnevnik (Bulgaria)">Dnevnik</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/24_Chasa" title="24 Chasa">24 Chasa</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-356" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-356">&#91;353&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Bulgaria" title="Media of Bulgaria">Bulgarian media</a> were described as generally unbiased in their reporting in the early 2000s and print media had no legal restrictions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200618,_23_357-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress200618,_23-357">&#91;354&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-landscape_358-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-landscape-358">&#91;355&#93;</a></sup> Since then, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_press" title="Freedom of the press">freedom of the press</a> has deteriorated to the point where Bulgaria scores 111th globally in the World Press Freedom Index, lower than all European Union members and membership candidate states. The government has diverted EU funds to sympathetic media outlets and bribed others to be less critical on problematic topics, while attacks against individual journalists have increased.<sup id="cite_ref-RSF_359-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RSF-359">&#91;356&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian1_360-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian1-360">&#91;357&#93;</a></sup> Collusion between politicians, oligarchs and the media is widespread.<sup id="cite_ref-RSF_359-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RSF-359">&#91;356&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_cuisine" title="Bulgarian cuisine">Bulgarian cuisine</a> is similar to those of other Balkan countries and demonstrates a strong Turkish and Greek influence.<sup id="cite_ref-Cuisine_361-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cuisine-361">&#91;358&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yogurt" title="Yogurt">Yogurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lukanka" title="Lukanka">lukanka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banitsa" title="Banitsa">banitsa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shopska_salad" title="Shopska salad">shopska salad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lyutenitsa" class="mw-redirect" title="Lyutenitsa">lyutenitsa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kozunak" class="mw-redirect" title="Kozunak">kozunak</a> are among the best-known local foods. Oriental dishes such as <a href="/wiki/Moussaka" title="Moussaka">moussaka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gyuvech" class="mw-redirect" title="Gyuvech">gyuvech</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Baklava" title="Baklava">baklava</a> are also present. Meat consumption is lower than the European average, given a notable preference for a large variety of salads.<sup id="cite_ref-Cuisine_361-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cuisine-361">&#91;358&#93;</a></sup> Bulgaria was the world\'s second-largest <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a> exporter until 1989, but has since lost that position.<sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362">&#91;359&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-363">&#91;360&#93;</a></sup> The 2016 harvest yielded 128 million litres of wine, of which 62 million was exported mainly to Romania, Poland and Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364">&#91;361&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mavrud" title="Mavrud">Mavrud</a>, Rubin, <a href="/wiki/Siroka_Melniska" title="Siroka Melniska">Shiroka melnishka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dimiat" title="Dimiat">Dimiat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Misket_Cherven" title="Misket Cherven">Cherven Misket</a> are the typical grapes used in <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_wine" title="Bulgarian wine">Bulgarian wine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-365">&#91;362&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rakia" title="Rakia">Rakia</a> is a traditional fruit <a href="/wiki/Brandy" title="Brandy">brandy</a> that was consumed in Bulgaria as early as the 14th century.<sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">&#91;363&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Bulgaria" title="Sport in Bulgaria">Sport in Bulgaria</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Grigor_Dimitrov_(18697714220).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Grigor Dimitrov in 2017" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Grigor_Dimitrov_%2818697714220%29.jpg/220px-Grigor_Dimitrov_%2818697714220%29.jpg" width="220" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Grigor_Dimitrov_%2818697714220%29.jpg/330px-Grigor_Dimitrov_%2818697714220%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Grigor_Dimitrov_%2818697714220%29.jpg/440px-Grigor_Dimitrov_%2818697714220%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2609" data-file-height="2637" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Grigor_Dimitrov_(18697714220).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Grigor_Dimitrov" title="Grigor Dimitrov">Grigor Dimitrov</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2015_Italian_Open_(tennis)" title="2015 Italian Open (tennis)">2015 Italian Open</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Bulgaria was among the countries appearing at the <a href="/wiki/1896_Summer_Olympics" title="1896 Summer Olympics">first modern Olympic games</a> in 1896, when it was represented by <a href="/wiki/Gymnastics_at_the_1896_Summer_Olympics" title="Gymnastics at the 1896 Summer Olympics">gymnast</a> <a href="/wiki/Charles_Champaud" title="Charles Champaud">Charles Champaud</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">&#91;364&#93;</a></sup> Since then, Bulgarian athletes have won 52 gold, 89 silver, and 83 bronze models,<sup id="cite_ref-368" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-368">&#91;365&#93;</a></sup> ranking 25th in the <a href="/wiki/All-time_Olympic_Games_medal_table" title="All-time Olympic Games medal table">all-time medal table</a>. <a href="/wiki/Olympic_weightlifting" title="Olympic weightlifting">Weight-lifting</a> is a signature sport for Bulgaria. Coach <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Abadjiev" title="Ivan Abadjiev">Ivan Abadzhiev</a> was instrumental in developing innovative training practices that have produced many Bulgarian world and Olympic champions in the sport since the 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-Sport_369-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sport-369">&#91;366&#93;</a></sup> Bulgarian athletes have also excelled in <a href="/wiki/Wrestling" title="Wrestling">wrestling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>, gymnastics, <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Sport_369-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sport-369">&#91;366&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stefka_Kostadinova" title="Stefka Kostadinova">Stefka Kostadinova</a> is the reigning <a href="/wiki/List_of_world_records_in_athletics" title="List of world records in athletics">world record</a> holder in the women\'s <a href="/wiki/High_jump" title="High jump">high jump</a> at 2.09 metres (6&#160;feet 10&#160;inches), achieved during the <a href="/wiki/1987_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="1987 World Championships in Athletics">1987 World Championships</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-370" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-370">&#91;367&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Grigor_Dimitrov" title="Grigor Dimitrov">Grigor Dimitrov</a> is the first Bulgarian tennis player in the Top 10 <a href="/wiki/ATP_Rankings#Current_rankings" title="ATP Rankings">ATP Rankings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-371" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-371">&#91;368&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular sport in the country by a substantial margin. The <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria_national_football_team" title="Bulgaria national football team">national football team</a>\'s best performance was a semi-final at the <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1994 FIFA World Cup">1994 FIFA World Cup</a>, when the squad was spearheaded by forward <a href="/wiki/Hristo_Stoichkov" title="Hristo Stoichkov">Hristo Stoichkov</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Sport_369-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sport-369">&#91;366&#93;</a></sup> Stoichkov is the most successful Bulgarian player of all time; he was awarded the <a href="/wiki/European_Golden_Shoe" title="European Golden Shoe">Golden Boot</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ballon_d%27Or" title="Ballon d&#39;Or">Golden Ball</a> and was considered one of the best in the world while playing for <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">FC Barcelona</a> in the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-372" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-372">&#91;369&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-373" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-373">&#91;370&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/PFC_CSKA_Sofia" title="PFC CSKA Sofia">CSKA</a> and <a href="/wiki/PFC_Levski_Sofia" title="PFC Levski Sofia">Levski</a>, both based in Sofia,<sup id="cite_ref-Sport_369-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sport-369">&#91;366&#93;</a></sup> are the most successful clubs domestically and <a href="/wiki/Eternal_derby_of_Bulgarian_football" title="Eternal derby of Bulgarian football">long-standing rivals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-374" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-374">&#91;371&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/PFC_Ludogorets_Razgrad" title="PFC Ludogorets Razgrad">Ludogorets</a> is remarkable for having advanced from the local fourth division to the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2014\xe2\x80\x9315 UEFA Champions League">2014\xe2\x80\x9315 UEFA Champions League</a> group stage in a mere nine years.<sup id="cite_ref-375" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-375">&#91;372&#93;</a></sup> Placed 39th in 2018, it is Bulgaria\'s highest-ranked club in <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-376" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-376">&#91;373&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<ul><li class="mw-empty-elt"></li>\n<li><a
